## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction. The rate of change of concentration (dA_dt) typically depends on the current concentration (A) through power-law, rational, or more complex functional forms. Time dependence may appear in non-elementary or externally driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (reaction with constant source/sink term)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (approach to equilibrium, A_eq = -c1/c0)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic reaction network)
- Logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (second-order with linear term)
- Consecutive reaction: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate in consecutive reactions)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated reaction rate)
- Rational quadratic: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (complex reaction mechanism)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Half-integer order: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (chain reaction mechanisms, radical kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple integer-order rate laws (1st, 2nd order) are most common in elementary reactions; non-integer orders suggest complex mechanisms or apparent rate laws
- If dA_dt depends only on A and not on t, the system is autonomous, indicating a closed chemical system with no external driving
- Rational function forms (A/(K+A)) indicate saturation behavior typical of enzyme catalysis or surface adsorption-limited reactions
- Negative values of dA_dt with positive A indicate consumption/decay; sign changes may indicate reversible reactions approaching equilibrium
- Polynomial dependence on A (e.g., c0*A + c1*A^2) often arises from parallel or competing reaction pathways
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law suggests non-autonomous effects such as photolysis, temperature ramps, or external reagent addition
- Square root dependence on concentration (A^0.5) is characteristic of chain reactions involving radical intermediates
- Products of concentration terms with different powers suggest lumped multi-step mechanisms where intermediates have been eliminated via quasi-steady-state approximation
- A rate law that is the ratio of polynomials in A typically arises from pre-equilibrium or steady-state approximation applied to multi-step mechanisms
